# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# LLVM Pass Manager Registration and Execution Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a new LLVM optimization pass is registered and executed in llvm/llvm-project. Find C++ source files that define: the PassManager template, the PassRegistry, the pass add() registration, and the pass execution order in the standard optimization pipeline (O2/O3).

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

43-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the LLVM pass registration and execution chain. Here's what I found:

## Summary

I've traced how LLVM optimization passes are registered and executed in the standard O2/O3 pipelines. The system consists of **8 key components**:

### Core Components:

1. **PassManager Template** - Manages sequences of passes with `addPass()` and `run()` methods
2. **PassConcept/PassModel** - Type-erased polymorphic dispatch system for storing different pass types
3. **PassRegistry** - Legacy registry for pass information and dependencies
4. **PassRegistry.def** - Macro-based registry of all available passes
5. **PassBuilder** - Central class for constructing optimization pipelines
6. **PassBuilderPipelines.cpp** - Implements the pipeline construction logic

### Execution Chain:

The **buildPerModuleDefaultPipeline()** function is the main entry point that:
1. Calls `buildModuleSimplificationPipeline()` to add early passes (SimplifyCFG, SROA, GlobalOpt, etc.)
2. Calls `buildModuleOptimizationPipeline()` to add main optimizations (inlining, loop optimizations, vectorization)

### Key Insight for O2/O3:

The passes are added in a specific order using `MPM.addPass()`, with O3 enabling additional passes like CallSiteSplitting. The PassManager executes them sequentially, wrapped in the polymorphic PassModel system that allows type-erased storage of different pass types.

The complete findings are saved in `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed file paths, symbol names, and a narrative explaining the entire registration and execution architecture.

If you want to use LLVM on multiple\\n36: /// threads simultaneously, you will need to use a separate PassRegistry on\\n37: /// each thread.\\n38: class PassRegistry {\\n39:   mutable sys::SmartRWMutex<true> Lock;\\n40: \\n41:   /// PassInfoMap - Keep track of the PassInfo object for each registered pass.\\n42:   using MapType = DenseMap<const void *, const PassInfo *>;\\n43:   MapType PassInfoMap;\\n44: \\n45:   using StringMapType = StringMap<const PassInfo *>;\\n46:   StringMapType PassInfoStringMap;\\n47: \\n48:   std::vector<std::unique_ptr<const PassInfo>> ToFree;\\n49:   std::vector<PassRegistrationListener *> Listeners;\\n50: \\n51: public:\\n52:   PassRegistry() = default;\\n53:   LLVM_ABI ~PassRegistry();\\n54: \\n55:   /// getPassRegistry - Access the global registry object, which is\\n56:   /// automatically initialized at application launch and destroyed by\\n57:   /// llvm_shutdown.\\n58:   LLVM_ABI static PassRegistry *getPassRegistry();\\n59: \\n60:   /// getPassInfo - Look up a pass' corresponding PassInfo, indexed by the pass'\\n61:   /// type identifier (&MyPass::ID).\\n62:   LLVM_ABI const PassInfo *getPassInfo(const void *TI) const;\\n63: \\n64:   /// getPassInfo - Look up a pass' corresponding PassInfo, indexed by the pass'\\n65:   /// argument string.\\n66:   LLVM_ABI const PassInfo *getPassInfo(StringRef Arg) const;\\n67: \\n68:   /// registerPass - Register a pass (by means of its PassInfo) with the\\n69:   /// registry. Not necessary with LTO post link pipelines since the pre link\n1135:   // pipeline already cleaned up the frontend output.\n1136:   if (Phase != ThinOrFullLTOPhase::ThinLTOPostLink) {\n1137:     // Do basic inference of function attributes from known properties of system\n1138:     // libraries and other oracles.\n1139:     MPM.addPass(InferFunctionAttrsPass());\n1140:     MPM.addPass(CoroEarlyPass());\n1141: \n1142:     FunctionPassManager EarlyFPM;\n1143:     EarlyFPM.addPass(EntryExitInstrumenterPass(/*PostInlining=*/false));\n1144:     // Lower llvm.expect to metadata before attempting transforms.\n1145:     // Compare/branch metadata may alter the behavior of passes like\n1146:     // SimplifyCFG.\n1147:     EarlyFPM.addPass(LowerExpectIntrinsicPass());\n1148:     EarlyFPM.addPass(SimplifyCFGPass());\n1149:     EarlyFPM.addPass(SROAPass(SROAOptions::ModifyCFG));\n1150:     EarlyFPM.addPass(EarlyCSEPass());\n1151:     if (Level == OptimizationLevel::O3)\n1152:       EarlyFPM.addPass(CallSiteSplittingPass());\n1153:     MPM.addPass(createModuleToFunctionPassAdaptor(\n1154:         std::move(EarlyFPM), PTO.EagerlyInvalidateAnalyses));\n1155:   }\n1156: \n1157:   if (LoadSampleProfile) {\n1158:     // Annotate sample profile right after early FPM to ensure freshness of\n1159:     // the debug info.\n1160:     MPM.addPass(SampleProfileLoaderPass(\n1161:         PGOOpt->ProfileFile, PGOOpt->ProfileRemappingFile, Phase, FS));\n1162:     // Cache ProfileSummaryAnalysis once to avoid the potential need to insert\n1163:     // RequireAnalysisPass for PSI before subsequent non-module passes.\n1164:     MPM.addPass(RequireAnalysisPass<ProfileSummaryAnalysis, Module>());\n1165:     // Do not invoke ICP in the LTOPrelink phase as it makes it hard\n1166:     // for the profile annotation to be accurate in the LTO backend.\n1167:     if (!isLTOPreLink(Phase))\n1168:       // We perform early indirect call promotion here, before globalopt.\n1169:       // This is important for the ThinLTO backend PGOIndirectCallPromotion(true /* IsInLTO */, true /* SamplePGO */));\n1174:   }\n1175: \n1176:   // Try to perform OpenMP specific optimizations on the module.
